I was glad to hear the heart-felt words of advice which *Gangādharraoji* has just given to our young students. The *Bhāgavata* also has given the same advice :

कौमारादाचरेत्प्राजः । धर्मान्भागवतान् हि तान् ।

“The wise should practise *Bhāgavata* - *Dharma* from the early age.” But we cannot say how far this advice would be really effective. Unless our heart feels an attachment for spiritual life and dislike for material pleasure, such advice would never be fruitful. As soon as the feeling of ‘dispassion’ arises in the heart, we must at once renounce everything and take up to spiritual life. Says the Upanisad :

यदहरेव विरजेत् तदहरेव प्रवृजेत् ।

“The moment the feeling of dispassion arises, that very moment one should renounce everything” and begin to practise spiritual *Sādhana*. Even though we feel dispassion in oldage, it does not matter. If we perform our *Sādhana* with proper intensity, God will surely bless us, even in our oldage. If *Gangādharraoji* performs *Nāmasmaraṇa*, for one or two years, with the same zeal and intensity, with which he served our nation for so many years, God will not fail to bless him, with His Grace.

(7)

**Gurudeva Ranade-My Father**

( *By : Smt. Vijaya V. Apte.* )

Almost a new era begins with the advent of Sri Gurudeva in the field of Indian Philosophy; or we may say that he is one of the brightest stars shining in the philosophical firmament of the resurgent India of the 20th century. His appearance on the scene was very necessary when India was undergoing the bewildering and dazzling changes by the contact with the Western Development of Science. A perplexed mind ultimately finds solace only when it is able to see within itself, with a heart full of faith, in the Ultimate Power. Thus the pathway to the philosophical and mystical sphere was opened by such illustrious seers who had shunned the bonds of old dogmatism. Here I can mention the names of Sri Ramakrishna Paramahamsa, Swami Vivekananda, Sri Rabindranath Tagore, Sri Aurobindo Ghosh, Dr. S. Radhakrishnan and Sri Gurudeva Ranade. Gurudeva Ranade was the builder of the modern spiritual empire. He stands before us as an intellectual and mystical collossus. As Dr. S. Radhakrishnan says- “ He taught not merely with his intellect but with his whole life. Philosophy

for him was not a profession but a consuming passion. My life is richer for having known him.” Even the Philosopher-King. like Dr. Radhakrishnan accepts Sri. Gurudeva as the unparalleled Mystic of the day.

Recently Dr. Burch from America ( Head of the Deptt. of Philosophy, Massachusetts University ) wrote : “ Had not Providence brought me to this venerable man, probably the most spiritually advanced person I shall ever know—to whom I was already bound by ties of mutual affection in order that he should be my spiritual preceptor ? ”

The world is verily aware of his unique greatness. Still it can know only the outward appearance of such uncomman personalities; as Sri Ramdas says,

गुप्त आहे उदंड वन, काय जाणती सेवक जन ।
तयासी आहे ते ज्ञान, वाह्यात्काराचे ॥

Now that we have lost such a precious diamond, the only way left to us, is to enlighten ourselves with his writings and his teachings.

Writing unveils the Man. Gurudeva Ranade was a lover of deep study of any topic taken on hand—may be of Literature, Science, or Philosophy. He used to go to the original sources of the matter—nay, even of the ‘words’ also and that is why he could enhance the treasure of the ‘word-kingdom’. He coined many new words in the philosophical and mystical literature. He was a Seer-Scientist of life and an apostle of virtues. Moral character is the basis of all success. A real spiritual life can only be built on the moral basis. Thus virtues meant everything for him: “ Character is the milk of life. ”

There was no superficiality in his writings. He was a voluminous writer and contributed original doctrines to the

world of philosophy: Logical development, consistency, brevity and accuracy are the characteristics of his style making it unique. He used to sum up his ideas in the end so that the true lover of knowledge could get a clear picture of the views propounded in the beginning. His style was lucid. He had a mastery over English as well as over Latin, Greek and German. He was well acquainted with the sainty literature in almost all Indian Languages and all the more with that in the *Alma Mater* Sanskrit. A profound scholar of Sanskrit that he was, his *Magnum opus* "The Constructive Survey of Upanishadic Philosophy" gives many new interpretations of the original Sanskrit texts. He used to say that we should study every problem in the way of the Kantian Critique. All his writings are constructions through critical expositions. His was a synthesising approach. A spirit of reconciliation runs through all his literature. For example: we can see the five antinomies in the Gita reconciled only on a view of Reality which regards the realisation of God as the be-all and the end-all of all Existence. He himself says, "This mystical view of Reality alone will enable us to reconcile all the intellectual dogmas that have infested the philosophies of the world. What we feel and what we realise should alone constitute our philosophy" And all this can only be achieved by God-Devotion which is the central thread of all virtues. The Christian and the Platonic virtues are all shown to be arising from one guiding virtue viz "भक्ति," so too, the virtues enunciated in the Gita. Thus Devotion alone would lead to the realisation of Self which constitutes the foundation and the peak of all Thought and Existence. The final verdict on the two controversial doctrines in Indian Philosophy i. e ज्ञानेत्तरकर्म and ज्ञानकर्म-समुच्चय is that ज्ञान is not an event but a process. Thus Gurudeva Ranade combined in himself, in quite a unique way, the different roles of Literator, Philosopher and a great Mystic. He was a mystic all his life.

Simplicity was a significant trait of his personality. He

has an abounding love for all who came in contact with him-whosoever he may be, a prince or a man on the street. He had a special affection for the students who stayed with him. His love for his disciples is also well-known. Everyone who came near him, thought that he was loved most by Sri Gurudeva. That was the one and the only one feeling that everybody had for him His serene smile and sanctifying presence, spread peace, love and good-will everywhere. He appreciated only the virtues in others without noticing their drawbacks. He was a saint of this type:-

परगुण-परमाणून्पर्वतीकृत्य नित्यम्
निजहृदि विकसन्तः सन्ति सन्तः कियन्तः ॥

This gave an impetus to enhance the goodness in others. This is why all his disciples believed that their spiritual teacher loved them most.

How can I be an exception to the rule? Having the privilege of being his only daughter, I am sure that all the goodness and happiness I have achieved in my life are due to the blessings and dignified love that have been showered on me by His Grace. People may think that a mystic who has realised God will not be able to play his role properly as a father or as the head of the family just like a worldly man. All the saints and the intellectuals of the world, like Tukaram, Ramadas, Mira, Kabir or Socrates, quite justify the above statement. But I can say with pride that my father well synthesised the worldly & the spiritual heights. His was not mere Renunciation, but his was Renunciation in action. He remained in the world but was not of it, as the adage goes, पद्मपत्रमिवाम्भसा. My father never forgot his duty and love towards us. The only thing was that his ways of expression were altogether different from those of a common man. And that is why people thought, that he had no family-life at all.

On the contrary, I can declare that my father's attitude towards us was just the reverse to what others thought of us. लोके भाविले ते उलथविले. My revered mother and myself never expected of my Venerable Father an attitude of a common man, because we were quite aware that we were members of the family of a great Saint. We were actually living in the spiritual atmosphere that my father spread all round. Even the parrot in भन्डनमिश्र's house could speak fluent Sanskrit. Then what to say of the members of his family ? I am proud that we were ave. inhailing the spiritual atmosphere.

I shall now deal with the following topics :-

- 1. His view of worldly life.

- 2. His moral standard.

- 3. His spiritual backing.

- 4. Gurudeva as a Mystic.

Regarding his view of life, people very well know how from his childhood he had a keen bent of mind for God-Realisation. To describe his life as such, will take a lot of time and it has been already done by many a writer in Marathi, English and Kannada. To be brief, I would say that he led a very simple and noble life with uncommon ways. His nature was sweet and affectionate towards all who came near him, even with the poorest inmate of the house. He used to get annoyed at times, but got himself calmed down immediately. He appreciated everybody and praised his achievements. What to say of his only daughter ! I still remember his joy when I passed my first degree examination ! It is a very minor thing, but the expression of love and joy that he had for me is more valuable to me than any thing else in the world. Though he was not bound by etiquette, worldly ties, even then he used to observe the necessary etiquette without fail. Once when I asked him whether I should accept a post of a lecturer in Gwalior he wrote to me to seek the permission of my father-in-law, Sardar Apte-in the first place, and then to

accept the post. Once in Jamkhandi, his birthplace-in 1956, I delivered a lecture in a women's meeting. He was surprised to see the big audience and just for fun said, " *Śakē* " ( that was how he used to call me ) are you going to attract more people than I do ? " The death of my only younger brother, a child of three and half months, was a bolt from the blue to all of us. My mother was very seriously ill at that time. I was all alone. All of a sudden he came in and patted me, saying " *Śakē*, inscrutable are the ways of God. Why do you weep ? I am everything for you. " One cannot imagine what I felt when I saw the mountain of courage incarnated before me. यीरोदात्त that he was, his face was filled with the glow of Divine Luminosity. I will never forget this incident in my life. When I studied Sanskrit in my B. A. I read *Shakuntala*'s going to her husband's house in अभिज्ञान-शाकुन्तलम्. But when I left my dear father's place after my marriage, I was reminded of *Kalidas*'s words for *Shakuntala* :

यास्यत्यञ्च शकुन्तलेति हृदयं संस्पृष्टमुत्कण्ठया ।
कण्ठस्तंभितवाष्पवृत्तिकलुष चिन्ताजडं दर्शनम् ॥

वैकल्यं मम तावदीदृशमिदं स्नेहादरण्यौकसः ।
पीड्यते गृहिणः कथं नु तनयाविश्लेषदुःखैर्नवैः ॥

A Rṣi like *Kaṇwa* could not control his paternal feeling for the adopted child, then what to say of Gurudeva ! I

The disciples of Sri Gurudeva know how much importance he attached to high moral standard and how vehemently he used to keep to it. Morality according to him was the basis of perfect life. He had an utter disgust for the worldly show. He was full of a spirit of humbleness and led a life of tranquility, truth penance, insight, strength, and right pursuit. He himself says that unless these conditions are fulfilled, the

aspirant after spiritual life, may never hope to realise the Self. He never directly told what he was or what were his views, but a true thinker could discern his views, in his description of some great saints. And so mere moral preaching bears of moral practice could have no place in his schema. The meetings or the 'sittings', or the discourses which were held in his presence with his friends and disciples, were quite enough for our guidance and moral equipment. Actually I felt that whatever ज्ञान he imparted to the disciples in general, was meant for everybody's wellbeing. If not direct, it was an affectionate indirect guidance to me from my Revered Father. His moral standard was so high and his personality so hallowed that one could approach him only with humility.

Further his spiritual backing was all the more valuable. It is needless to say more about it because all his followers know how much spiritual support they received from their Guru. Should I not call it an exclusive privilege for me and my respected mother? Let me express here, that most of the spiritual discourses have not been missed by us. Towas ever secret they might have been or if I am to put it more frankly, every such secret discourse was arranged in such a manner that we could get guidance from it. After many days, all of a sudden, he used to ask my mother and myself some such questions regarding the earlier discourses, only to test whether we were attentive. The object was only to lead us towards the higher path of God-Realisation. He used to enlighten us sometimes with his rememberance of Guru Sri. Bhausaheb Maharaj, or sometimes silently with a spiritual experience. अनुभव. Once in 1956, when he was to go to Jamkhandi-he was having a spiritual discourse, with many *Sādhakās* at Nimbal. I was there, and all of a sudden an idea occured to my mind-'Sri Gurudeva is leaving this place to participate in the *Amīt Mahūtsava* to be held in his honour at Jamkhandi-and now who will protect Nimbal?' All of a sudden, I saw a lustrous halo encircling His Holy face.

and he was smiling serenely ! Thus he used to come to our rescue.

Lastly, come to Gurudeva as a Mystic. He says in his Karnatak Mysticism "Mysticism is a way of spiritual life which binds all humanity together." As I have said before, the world values him as a great Mystic and God-realiser. He was engrossed in meditation all the time except when he was doing intellectual work. Very little time was given for his routine work. He worked for the philosophical field so devotedly and undauntedly that he actually re-drafted a page eight days before his passing away. As Sri Radhakrishnan has apply said "He not merely taught philosophy but He lived it." The whole life of a Philosopher-Saint was thus spent in the pursuit of God-realisation with rational, direct, personal, and spiritual experience. All the philosophical works-the Constructive Survey and the three Pathways in Karnatak, Maharashtra and Hindi Literatures, the Gita as the Philosophy of God-realisation, and the other works of his, go to show his profound, life-long study and intuitive experience. "Mind is purified, Intellect is clarified and the Soul is sanctified by the study of the Gita." He says elsewhere: "A state of Beatificism is itself our liberation. It is not to be found after death, but here and now. Mysticism denotes that attitude of mind which involves a direct, immediate, firsthand intuitive apprehension of God". This he says on the strength of his own moral, spiritual and mystical experiences. But "this state of God-realisation is due to the कृपा of the spiritual teacher सदगुरु," said Sri Gurudeva. "The preceptor who shows the Truth in its real form is called a *Sad-Guru*;" सत्याचे गुप्त रूप जो दाखवतो तो सदगुरु. 'This view is upheld by all the great mystics of the world: ज्ञानेश्वर, तुकाराम, कबीर, महिमति, पुरन्दरदास, St. Teresa, Plotinus and others. He led a pure life of mysticism and taught a full-fledged morality for the individual and life of Absolute Good to society. If each and everybody could achieve his own

Good by following the mystical path, then one day, the whole world would surely and unmistakably reach the Ultimate Good. Thus we see that He placed Mysticism on a Pure Philosophical basis. His writings prove him to be a Grammarian of Mysticism. परमार्थपाणिनि. Whatever the knowledge we have achieved about the mystical methods is only due to, I am sure, the affectionate and spiritual guidance of a great Saint-Father. One cannot judge the merits of a great man unless one lives in close touch with him for many days in continuity. In that respect I am fortunate enough to have spent most of my life - time with him. What to say of my respected mother who has lived and let live others with him for 40 years. To be fully aware of the greatness of a great man, one must become like him.

तुका म्हणे अगे व्हावे ते आपण.
तरीच माहमान येईल कळो।

It is not possible and is not at all practicable for a common man. Even then some idea of His greatness is gained by being the member of his saintly family. I am rather forced to conclude here because the flow of these spiritual remembrances is unending. I am reminded here of Longfellow's unforgetable lines-

“ Lives of Great men all remind us
We can make our life sublime,
And departing leaves behind us
Foot-prints on the sands of time. ”

My most Revered Father has built the Spiritual Empire- and has shown us the Divine Path to be followed rationally. Thus he has left behind him for the aspirants a vast legacy of Divine Brotherhood to catch up the “ Pilot Perenial ”.

(8)

## How I Found My Gurudeva

( By : Dr. N. S. Christian )

A seeker of Truth since my boyhood, with Religion and Philosophy, Mysticism and Yoga as my hobby, I have been a friend of *sādhus* and *fukeers*. Often I fell a victim of deception and fraud; still the orange-clad attraction swayed over me. I read a large number of books and visited *āśramas* in search of mystic knowledge. I have a profound regard for our Land of Wisdom, its unbroken chain of saints and sages, the Ancient Scriptures and our rich cultural and spiritual heritage.

During those days I had been practising Kundalinī Yoga without a Guru to guide me, by just following instructions given in books on the subject. One night, during my deep meditation, I experienced a terrible psychic shock, pertaining to the rising of Kundalinī-Śakti, the details of which are too long to be recorded here. Since then, I had experienced a strange mental and bodily distress, ranging from a sense of fulness and intoxication to a fear of impending death, with fluctuations in my pulse, and varied and vague symptoms,

probably due to a disturbance of my autonomic nervous system. Sleep had completely disappeared and often I got into ecstatic states and trances with the development of visual and auditory signs pertaining to Yoga. My friends, who took me on a jeep to Ganeshpuri, have been witnessing them during our journey. We visited Swāmi Nityānanda late in the evening and I implored him to bless me. He placed his hand on my head and exclaimed, "Acchā, Jāv, Abhī milegā Jāv". We reached Bombay late at night and rested at the Archaeological guest rooms situated on the Fort at Sion. The next morning was Āṣādha-Ekādaśī. I woke up early at 4 A. M. and was reciting "Lalitā-Sahasra-Nāma". My friends were snoring in their slumber after the tirescome jeep-drive the previous day, a distance of 250 miles in torrential rain all along the journey. On reaching the closing lines which mean, "Imperishable embodiment of compassion, Light in my darkness" etc. while reciting the thousand names of The Divine Mother of the Universe, I fell into a trance and lost myself in ecstacy with a vision of the Mother. My friends woke up to see me moaning with a flushed face, my eyes pouring out tears. They were greatly perturbed until I recovered after nearly half an hour. The whole day I was in a blissful state. Dr. Kulkarni noted fluctuation in my pulse and he took me to our friend, Dr. Tulpule, eminent cardiologist and Professor of Medicine at the J. J. Medical College, residing at Dadar, himself a great devotee and a pious soul. The learned doctor found nothing abnormal in me. The cardiogram and X-Ray revealed a perfect heart. I was experiencing a sense of fulness and intoxication and a feeling that my body would burst out. I requested the Doctor to prescribe medicine. Dr. Tulpule advised me to see Gurudeva Ranade of Nimbal and said that there was nothing wrong with me. We returned home. I continued my Sādhana and had two memorable dreams. The first was Śrī Nityānanda who took me on his lap and threatened to slap me when I suddenly woke up. The second was Gurudeva Ranade, whom I had never seen before, appearing and telling me in Marathi,

“Doctor. tumi Nimbālalā yā, mī samādhi - yogu dākhavito” meaning, “Doctor, you come to Nimbal. I will teach you Samādhi-Yoga.”

Three weeks later. I went to Nimbal with my friend Deshpande guided by Dr. S. G. Tulpule, *M. A.*, *Ph. D.*, Head of the Department of Marathi, Poona University, the illustrious biographer of the Great Master, and who happens to be a cousin of his name-sake in Bombay. At the ‘Abode of Peace’ I found my Master, the Divinest Soul I have ever met. His mystic touch set me free from all my spiritual ailments. Every-time I visited the *Āśrama*, I rejoiced in the sanctity, aura and affection of Gurudeva. He graciously initiated me in the Supreme Yoga of Meditation on God’s Name. He gave me Christa-Nāma without distracting me from my *lṣṭa-Devatā* and added me to his large family of devoted disciples.

Gurudeva Ranade’s writings on mysticism and Yoga are masterly, revealing the highest attainments in the History of Speculative Philosophy. He has placed before the aspirant, secrets of incalculable value, effectively leading him into the ‘Pathway to God’. His comparative study of the mystics of different lands and religions, is extremely fascinating and informative. His original method of explaining difficult themes in simple language is unique, depicting in a systematic manner, the incentives, preparatory methods, experiences and achievements of the Saints and Sages of all ages and countries with the sources of his writings which are so full and complete. His ‘Survey of Upaniṣadic Philosophy’ is a scholarly exposition of the truth and richness that came out of the Age of The *Āraṇyakas*. His incomparable treatise on the *Gītā* as a Philosophy of God - realisation is a work of great value to a *Sādhaka* on the Pathway to God. The book gives in a nutshell, the various commentaries on the Greatest Scripture of Spiritual India, and through the different views expressed by the various scholars and devotees of the Lord of Kurukṣetra, Gurudeva Ranade places before a student of Yoga, the avenues of

God-realisation and the diverse forms in which God reveals Himself to a seeker.

Gurudeva Ranade was a Saint who conquered hunger and thirst. He proved in his life what Christ had said, that "Man doth not live by bread alone". For many years he was sustaining himself on a few cups of tea a day. He defied bodily ailments and refused all medicines and treatment when he happened to be ill. As the Risis of Old, he shunned publicity and lived to perfection, the teaching. "Let thy light so shine before men that they may see thy good works and glorify thy Father who is in Heaven."

The afternoon of my arrival at Nimbal, I was sitting in a gathering of devotees with Gurudeva Ranade inspiring and thrilling us with his Spiritual discourses. All of a sudden he summoned me affectionately to his side and asked me to recite a sacred hymn. During my recitation of a verse from the works of the Saints of Saiva Siddhānta, I fell into a trance with the experience of Samādhi which Gurudeva had promised me in a dream. When I regained myself, I found lying down in ecstasy, with my eyes full of tears of joy, and my head on the lap of my Master who sprinkled water on my face and was passing his frail hands on my back. I got up and sat when he asked me, "Is that what you wanted?" I replied, "I do not know. Gurudeva I But whatever you have given me, is a blessing". I returned home and one night, after my meditation, in a semi-sleep state, I saw Gurudeva in front of me. He said to me, "Doctor, your head is full of some worms and I shall remove them" and he pulled out long thready worms from my left ear and threw them out. Ever since that memorable event, all those disturbing symptoms which I had developed after my shock during Kundalini-Yoga disappeared for ever. Then I realised the beauty of having a Spiritual Master and appreciated the writings of the Great Sanikarā-cārya on the subject. Thus I met my Gurudeva.

With the dazzling brilliance of the Rising-Sun, the Master's face reflected the vast Universe. Everytime I sat beside him amidst the devotees at Nimbal with his favourite green shawl covering his body, he appeared to me to have resembled The Ancient Mystic Parrot, reciting the Infallible Vedas. He has been a perfect preceptor after the Ideal of Śri Śrikarācārya's Vivekacūdāmāṇi description of a Guru, without the slightest taint of human egoism. He was an embodiment of humility.

The Spirit of The Universe, encased in a pale ivory frame and a frail body, mostly skin and bone, Gurudeva Ranade resembled a feather-stripped bird, a pair of God-intoxicated eyes, glowing compassionately in their hallowed sockets, situated below elevated eye-brows, the symbol of triumph in his life-long *tapasvā*, an extremely affectionate heart, tirelessly pouring out its life-giving nectar of Spiritual Wisdom in warbling words of divine melody. Gurudeva was a self-sustained Angel of The Lord in brief, "God in flesh and blood."

The Master has left us and departed to the Abode of the gods whom he resembled, "Mingled after death, with the Whole Universe, whose voice is on the rolling air and who stands in the Rising Sun and who may be seen in star or flower or wherever the eyes may be cast."

"He is made one with nature : there is heard
His voice in all her music, from the moan
Of thunder to the song of the night's sweet bird;
He is a presence to be felt and known
In darkness and in light, from herb and stone,
Spreading itself wherever that Power may move
Which has withdrawn his being to its own;
Which wields the world with never-wearied love,
Sustains from beneath and kindles it above."

(9)

## Angelic Personality

( *By : S. N. L. Shrivastava* )

Whoever has come in contact with Dr. R. D. Ranade cannot forget him till the end of his life. His was an angelic personality, radiating joy and peace and spiritual light. An electric smile ever played on his lips and his eyes shone with a brightness reflecting in inner illumination. I never found him ruffled or sour or bitter or stooping to petty things. He was above all narrow considerations of caste, creed and community. People felt uplifted in his presence and the more one came in contact with him the more he sought his presence. He was an *ajātashatru* ( one who had no enemies ), and a friend of everybody ( *sarveṣām yo suhṛnnityah* ), a seraphic soul “ with malice toward none and charity for all. ”

When Dr. Ranade came to Nagpur to deliver the University Extension Lectures on the Bhagwad-Gita sometime before 1930 ( I do not remember the exact year ), I had the first opportunity of seeing and listening to him. I was then an undergraduate student in the Government College there, then known

as the Morris College. I had offered Sanskrit and Philosophy for my B. A. Examination and was particularly interested in philosophy. I do not think I followed Dr. Ranade's lectures very closely; but his personality and erudition impressed me. I still remember how my attention was particularly rivetted on Dr. Ranade's explanation of the sentence of the Gita *adyṣta-poorvam hrṣitosmi dīstvā bhayena ca pravyathita mano me*. Explaining this sentence Dr. Ranade said that when a mystic has his first vision he is beside with joy but also overwhelmed with fear at the unprecedented sight. The confident tone in which Dr. Ranade spoke smiling joyfully all the time, assured me that his explanation was backed by his own mystical exoerience at first hand. I could not help feeling that I was in the presence of a man who was not only an erudite scholar but a man of spiritual illumination as well. I decided to join the Allahabad University for my post-graduate studies in Philosophy. During the academic sessions 1931-32 and 1932-33, I was a post-graduate student of philosophy under Dr. R. D. Ranade at the Allahabad University. It was during these years that I came in very intimate contact with him, meeting him very frequently, sometimes almost every day.

Ranade was a teacher of teachers. He had his own method of finding out the abilities of students. To all students who joined the post-graduate classes in philosophy he asked them to write philosophical essays of their own choice. On my joining I wrote an essay on the Mandukyopaniṣad under the caption "The Psychological Basis of Advaitism". Prof. Ranade was beside with joy when he read it. "What is your age?" he asked me. "21, Sir" I replied. "No" he said, "Your age is 42, for your essay avinces miturity of that age." He at once forwarded that essay with a note for publication in the *Vedanta Kesari*, Madras, where it was duly published. That was my first philosophical publication.

Once I approached him for suggesting me books on Modern Western Philosophy. He gave me a lengthy list of

books, pointing out particular chapters in many of the books where particular topics were notably dealt with. I was simply astounded by the vastness and thoroughness of his learning. Ranade was global in his outlook. Though deeply rooted in Indian thought and culture, he was abreast of the latest currents of thought in Western Philosophy of his times. He always advocated a "correlated study of Eastern and Western Philosophies."

Philosophy with Ranade was not merely an intellectual pursuit, but also as he often used to say, a way of life. In his own way of life, Ranade was, to my mind, an exemplar of a true Indian philosopher.

### Evening Meditations at Draupadighat

Gurudeva Ranade's life was a life of absorption in meditation. He was a Dhyan-Yogi *par excellence*. I can best describe his life as a person fication of the following verse of the Bhagwad-Gita :

विविक्षासेवो लव्वाशो यत्राक्षायमानसः ।

ध्यानयोगपरो नित्य वैराग्यं समुपाश्रितः ॥ - B.G.18-52

Every evening Prof. Ranade used to go out in his car to the banks of the Ganges at Draupadighat for quiet meditation for some time. He would take us also with him. When the car reached the chosen spot, Prof. Ranade would ask everybody seated therein to get down and stroll along at some distance till the horn of the car was blown which was a signal for us all to return to him. The horn sounded and we would then all be seated again with Prof. Ranade in the car and return home. This was a daily practice.

Prof.Ranade's bungalow at Allahabad was a rendezvous for the meeting of all aspiring souls of all ranks in life. In

these gatherings sparks from the anvil of his luminous mind would often fly and enkindle spiritual fire in the hearts of the assembled. On one occasion he said in a very serious mood: "We must fill our lives with God I" On another occasion he said forcefully: "We must implant our feet firmly on the back of time," meaning thereby that we must transcend the time-consciousness and rise to an awareness of the ETERNAL NJW.

Dr. Ranade would receive all visitors to him very kindly and gracefully and would invariably offer tea. I never found him assuming airs before anybody.

Gurudeva is physically no more with us but the memory of his seraphic life shall ever remain green in our minds.

(10)

## Mysterium Tremendum

( *By : Prof. S. K. Gupta* )

A sketch of a God-realiser by one who is not so is hardly adequate. Unless the spiritual depth which Ranade attained is fathomed, one can hardly depict him appropriately. Before I attempt a description of Ranade from the standpoint of a non-realiser of God, I bow down in veneration to the 'Mysterium Tremendum' that is Ranade.

I had the privilege of being his disciple for two years at the University of Allahabad. He taught Indian Philosophy in M. A. ( previous ) class. I still remember his explanation of 'Tajjalan' – the cryptic word from Chhandogya Upanishad. That from which all things originate, into which they are ultimately resolved and in which they live and have their being is 'Tajjalan.' All powers in this universe, physical or mental, are manifestations of His energy. He is the essence of all beings. One who realises Him finds Him in all beings. As the Gita says. He abides in all multiplicity undivided.

Sarbabhutesu jenaikam bhāvamabyayam iksate
Abibhaktam bibhaktesu tajjnanam biddi sattvikam

( Chapter 18, verse 20 )

The full import of the term ' Tajjalan ' only a mystic can realise. And a mystic can explain it the best. Even though the listeners are non-mystics and so cannot enter much deep into its meaning, yet they are impressed. They are aware of a grand presence. An impression of a life time is created.

His success as a teacher was manifest all the more at the level of guiding research. It was a privilege to be a research scholar under his guidance. Original ideas and scholarly dissertations are specialities. First rate theses and books by research scholars are the outcome of his guidance. Dr. Chandra Dhar Sharma, the Author of that excellent book ' A Critical Survey of Indian Philosophy ', was a research scholar under Ranade's guidance, when I was a student of M. A. Class. His book contains scholarly dissertations and views of Ranade. I happened to meet him, when he came to Orissa as the President of All Orissa Philosophy Association. He agreed with me that his book contains Ranade's views, which add much to its excellence.

Not only his scholarship but also his unassuming nature that made Ranade an attractive personality. It was a pleasure to meet him at his lodge. His affable nature and sparkling humour made his company enjoyable. One has the sense of something special about him. And yet during my two years stay at Allahabad, I could never know that he was a God-realiser. Several years after I passed out from Allahabad University, I happened to read his epoch making book ' Pathway

सर्वभूतेषु येनैकं भावमव्ययमीक्षत ।
अविभक्तं विभक्तेषु तज्ज्ञानं विद्धि सात्त्विकम् ॥

to God in Hindi Literature ”. I realised then that he was God-realiser. A book on God written by a God-realiser has an amazing depth and a wonderful charm. The reader realises, that here is something above the ordinary. Such a book stands out from other books on God, written by non-realisers. There is a book on contemporary Indian Philosophy, wherein the Philosophies of eminent modern philosophers of India including Ranade are given, through their own writings. I noticed therein that Ranade's essay surpassed all other essays in depth. The other essays have high philosophical acumen, but not the depth of Ranade, which is the outcome of God-realisation. All the books written by Ranade are outstanding. They bear the stamp of his deep spiritual insight. Though he is physically no more, one can feel the influence of that liberated soul, through his books. It can lead a person to immortality.

## ( II )

### A Glimpse of His Samadhi

( By : Sri. V. G. Jamkhandi )

It was some time in NOVEMBER 1954. Sri Gurudev Ranade was at Dharwar for a few days for delivering lectures on " PATHWAY to GOD in KANNAD LITERATURE " under the auspices of the Karnatak University. It was my rare privilege to be with him during this period.

I was initiated by Sri Gurudev Ranade only a few months before in July and I did not know much about his habits and modes of meditation. However, intimation had been given to me by senior Sadhakas that he would like to go out for meditation in a car. Accordingly, a car was kept ready for him so that it could be available any time he desired.

On the very first day after his arrival at Dharwar, at about 11.15 A. M., Sri. Gurudev said he would go out for meditation. He took with him a disciple-Sri. Bhaurao Nimbargi and also asked me to accompany him. So Sri Gurudev sat on the right side in the back seat and I was on the left side. Sri. Bhaurao Nimbargi and the driver were in the front seat. After

we drove about a mile along the Belgaum road, Shri Gurudev asked the driver to stop immediately. He had a peculiar and rather, inexplicable, way of asking the driver, in quick succession, to turn to right or left and then stop abruptly and only an expert driver could correctly follow his instructions. On one occasion, it happened that the car was stopped blocking the passage for other vehicles. but nothing came that way until his "Nema" was finished. After the car was stopped, Sri. Gurudev asked the driver and Sri Nimbargi to get down for some time, but asked me to sit for "Nema" — meditation there only along with him. I thought it was a rare opportunity for me to sit within 2-3 feet of Sri. Gurudev for meditation, though I must frankly confess, I hardly knew then what real meditation meant.

I then saw a most wonderful sight, which I had no occasion to see before, and have not been privileged to see thereafter. Sri Gurudev started uttering loudly and continuously "NARAYAN, NARAYAN", and, within a minute he went into complete SAMADHI and seemed to be fast asleep. I was overwhelmed by a feeling of awe, reverence and wonder I had only read about Samadhi which great saints like Sr Ramakrishna Paramahaunsa are said to have experienced. but, I had never seen any one actually going into Samadhi. About 20 minutes later, Sri. Gurudev opened his eyes and said he had very good "Nema"—meditation—and asked me to call the driver and start back.

As soon as the car started, Sri. Gurudev asked Sri Bhaurao Nimbargi to recite some song and to my very great surprise he recited one by the great saint Purandaradas, in which the Divine Name given to me by Sri. Gurudev was eulogiged and was said to be the rarest privilege for any human being to secure. By the time the song was finished we reached home.

This is what happened and the whole episode, the context of facts and close sequence, has made an indelible

impression on my consciousness. I am not going to offer any explanation for it, but my feeling is one of the most respectful and deepest gratitude to my SAD-GURU who, out of his infinite compassion, was pleased to give me an actual demonstration of spiritual samadhi, which could be attained by meditation on the Divine Name. He was also graciously pleased to convey to me, through the song of saint Purandardas, the unsurpassed potency and significance of the Divine Name and this conviction has been strengthened and reinforced in me during all this period and now it has veritably become a part and parcel of my being.

(12)

## Come for Nama alone

( By : *Sri J. V. Purulekar* )

I had gone to Nimbal and was staying in a room, occupied by the late Dr. Padaki and Shri Sondur. Shri Aroskar also came there from Vengurla, probably for the first time. This was in 1953 and one day, we all had our lunch at about 7 p. m. 'Nucchu' ( small pieces of Jowar bread soaked in butter milk ) was served to all the persons. There was no other dish. Shri Aroskar, who was sitting by my side, enquired whether rice would be served and received a negative reply. Jowar bread was prepared; but it was not to be served until the whole stock of 'nucchu' was exhausted. Jowar bread was welcome to me but not 'nucchu'. When 'nucchu' was served for the second time, Shri Aroskar and I did not receive it. Shri Aroskar did not relish 'nucchu' at all and when we came out of the hall for washing our hands, he remarked : " I cannot continue to stay here any longer, if rice was not available. " I looked at him and said, " I too do not like 'nucchu'. "

The next day at about 3-30 a. m. Shri Sondur and I got

up and we sat for ' Nema ' ( meditation on the Name of God. ) Dr. Padaki continued to have sleep till about 6 A. M. and when we ended our ' Nema ' just about that time, he told us that he had no good sleep on account of bugs and mosquitoes and showed rashes on his arms. He asked us how we did not suffer from mosquito bites and how we could sit quietly for ' Nema. ' I replied him that I had good ' Nema ' from 3-30 a. m. to which he said, " You are lucky. "

That day in the afternoon, we were having a ' sitting ' ( Satsang ) in the Dhyana-Mandir. Shri Gurudev was present. About 25 sadhaks, including Professor Damle, were present. It was about 2 p. m. Shri Gurudev pointed his fingers to two of the old sadhaks and said to them, " You were always moving with Maharaj (i. e. Sri Bhausaheb Maharaj). You tell us some reminiscences about him. " Shri Hanmantrao Kannur then told us the following story.

It was in about 1904, one day morning. Shri Maharaj, as usual took a pot of water, left his room and proceeded towards open fields to ease himself. We both followed him with pots of water in our hands. We crossed some distance; prickly pear had grown nere and there. Maharaj reached a spot where there was a small piece of stony land and he suddenly sat down for ' Nema ' on that spot. As there was prickly pear round about, we put down our pots and stood up, looking at Maharaj. He was fully absorbed in ' Nema '. Just then a scorpion entered on the body of Maharaj. Our heart beats became fast; we became nervous and were perspiring. What, if it stings? that was our fear. We were gazing at it. Maharaj had given us instructions that he must never be disturbed when he was in ' Nema. ' So we could not remove the scorpion from his body. Slowly, it got down from the other side and went away. Thereafter, when Maharaj got up we asked him, " Maharaj, " is this a place suitable for ' Nema ' ? Maharaj replied, " What can I do ? I was helpless. As soon as I reached this

spot. I was compelled to sit down for "Nema." That was the God's wish." And then, he enquired of us why we asked such a question. We then narrated to Maharaj how the scorpion entered upon his body and how we became nervous and added. if it had stung you, how painful it would have been? Maharaj then smiled and said, "When I was in 'Nema' was it my human body? No, no, it was God's and how can the scorpion dare sting God?"

At this stage, Shri Gurudev stopped the two sadhaks, looked at Dr. Padaki and addressed the gathering:

"Look here. There are persons here who complain that the bugs and mosquitoes bite them and that therefore they are not having "Nama." They do not even care to get up and sit down for "Nema." Absorb yourself in "Nema" and even the scorpion would not sting. What of mosquitoes?"

Dr. Padaki looked at me and suggested to me that this talk was meant for him. He felt very sorry. He became quite punctual in his "Nema" thereafter and was very much advanced on the Pathway to God.

Shri Gurudev then asked one of the Sadhaks to sing a song. The man started to sing about Shri Krishna and Sudama. Sudama goes to Shri Krishna with a handful of parched rice as present. Shri Krishna receives him with all affection and dignity and gives him full honours. Shri Krishna then asks Sudama, "What have you brought for me to eat?" Sudama hesitated to tell him that only a handful of parched rice was with him. Shri Krishna presses Sudama, who at last produces the parched rice. Shri Krishna jumps to receive it and eats with relish.

At this point, Shri Gurudev stopped the song, looked at Shri Aroskar and said to the sadhaks, "If you want to stay

**Rambhan Mahara**

here and grow in spiritual advancement, here you will get Sudama's parched rice only. "Nucchu" you will get here. you must eat it with relish and spend your time in "Nema." I give you what I can afford—Sudama's parched rice, Nucchu. You come here for "Nema" and not for good and spicy food.

The sitting ended at about 5 p. m. when Shri Gurudev. left the Dhyna-Mandir for his bath.

(13)

Gurudev As I saw him.

( *By I P. Singh* )

It was the spring of 1951. A fellow student of Philosophy Department in Allahabad University informed me that Prof. R. D. Ranade was going to give a talk on "Mysticism in Hindi Literature" later in the evening. I had heard a great deal about Prof. Ranade—as Head of the Department of Philosophy, as Dean of the Faculty of Arts and as Vice Chancellor of the University. I also had read some of his published works. But, I had never met him till that time. Even though I had an instinctive conviction that mysticism had reached great heights in Hindi poetry, I did not feel much attracted by the topic of the lecture. The desire to meet Prof. Ranade was, however, so powerful that I made it a point to attend the lecture. For some reason I don't remember, I reached late. When I entered the hall, the speaker was explaining the significance of Meera Bai's famous Bhajan - "*Jogi mat ja mat ja*". He was talking about a most crucial line of this bhajan. The earlier part of this line meant : "The path of love and devotion is strange." The latter part had two known versions : "*Mujh*

*ko gail bata ja* ' and ' *Mujh ko gail lagaja*. ' meaning " You show me the way " and " you escort me along the way ". Prof. Ranade was explaining how the difference between these two versions symbolized the two systems of spiritual discipline in this country, namely, the path of knowledge and the path of complete submission and identification with God.

This deep analysis, given in clear and simple words, in the characteristic swift delivery of Prof. Ranade, in which a lot of meaning was given by the expression upon his face rather than words, made me feel for the first time in my life that I was face to face with a sage, who deserved to be in line of the seers whom this country has produced since times immemorial. Thereafter. I kept a close watch on his speaking programmes and made an effort to see that I did not miss any of his lectures. But, this was not enough for me. Through a close friend of mine, who used to visit the residence of Prof. Ranade, I reached his place within a few weeks of my meeting him for the first time. Thereafter, I did not miss any excuse for going to his house. In the evenings, his drawing room used to be full of high dignitaries - senior Government officials, Judges of High Courts, Ministers of States and Central Government and big political leaders. The thing which impressed me most in these gatherings at his house was the absence of any forbidding sense of alcoholness or artificial mystery which people of lesser spiritual merit in this country tend to create around themselves.

For the next two years, I continued to see the great thinker, who was also an accomplished speaker and an expert in social engineering. But the craving in my mind to know Ranade the man, remained unfulfilled till the spring of 1954. When I became a lecturer in the Department of Philosophy, Ganga Natha Jha Hostel where I was staying asked me to quit the place as I was no more a student. Some friends of mine invited me to stay with them. But I instead, asked my friend,

Safish Chandra Verma, to explore the possibility of our staying with him. The same evening Safish came to me to say that Prof. Ranade had agreed to our request It was an unbelievable news and I shifted forthwith. I knew the discipline of staying in the house which without so boasting was an Ashram in the true sense. We all slept on thin durries on the ground and ate the simple meal prepared in the household kitchen. Of course, these things were not compulsory. However, the atmosphere in the house was such that we all felt happy and elevated in leading such a life. It was in a surrounding like this that in my inner most heart, I accepted Prof. Ranade as my Guru.

Gurudev used to be in meditation for hours every day. Occasionally, Madhukar Kumthekar would ask me to lead some special visitors to his room. I keenly awaited such opportunities. While it was not necessary for me to wait, once the visitors were in, I used to linger inside as long as possible, in an effort to imbibe as much of Gurudev's presence as possible. Gurudev as the host in his drawing room was completely different from what he was in his private room. His was an indescribable presence which caused an over-powering sensation on those who were around. Occasionally, he would only look at the persons for quite a few seconds before starting to talk. During this silence, one got the impression as if he was communicating.

The most striking feature of Gurudev's personality was his ability to talk and to think at the level of the person with whom he was at any time. It was an exhilarating experience to see the great mystic discussing the grossest problems of the people around him. On many occasions, I saw him agitated over the domestic problems of his peon-Bhagwan Deen, who used to live in the servant quarters and was like the Grand Chamberlain of the house-hold. It gave an ironical delight to see this great man upset over the fact that Bhagwan

Deen's cow had not been traced or his son had fared poorly in his school. Once these problems were resolved, Gurudev expressed a childlike happiness. Similar problems, personal and official, used to come to him from various quarters. He had time for every one.

Alongside lecturing in the University, I was also preparing for the Indian Administrative Service and Indian Foreign Service examinations. Gurudev used to ask me from time to time how my preparations were going. Early in 1955, when the results of the competitive examinations came out, I was in a dilemma whether to join the Indian Foreign Service, in which my name was first in the list or the Indian Administrative Service. I took my problem to Gurudev. He solved it for me in no time. He told me that knowing my temperament he would advise me to join the Foreign Service. I touched his feet and sent my reply to the Government of India. In the month of April, he gave me a most touching send-off to Delhi. I had an occasion to see him a year later. In between I was engaged. I sent him a letter seeking his blessings while entering the life of a householder. After my marriage, I visited Allahabad with my bride to receive his Āshirvād. That meeting turned out to be our last as I left India a few weeks later for training in diplomacy at the Oxford University. Gurudev blessed us. He told me that in my service abroad I must remember always the great cultural heritage of India. I left him with the promise to see him as soon as I returned from my foreign tour.

At Oxford during 1956-57, Madhukar wrote occasionally to me about Gurudev's further studies in mysticism in Marathi and Kannada literatures. One morning I went to Blackwells, the well-known booksellers in Oxford, and requested them to order a complete set of Gurudev's writings for me. I returned in the evening to my room to find a letter from Madhukar informing me that Gurudev was no more. I cried like a child as I have done on very few occasions, indeed,

Our country's greatest wealth has been the unbroken chain of our saints and seers. While I have respect for thinkers and holy men whom I have personally met, I have an instinctive revulsion from god-men who are surrounded by a fence of pre-fabricated holiness. I am of the view that it is much easier for an ordinary man to appear saintly than it is for a saint to appear human. Gurudev Ranade carried his spiritual greatness in an invisible reservoir. The man in him was never sidetracked by the Sage.

(14)

( Dr. Ranade's Magnetic Attraction )

( By : S. L. Pandey )

व्याख्यातोपनिषत्तत्त्वं रहस्यवादभास्क म् ।
श्रीरानडेगुरुं वन्दे ज्ञानभक्तिजगद्गुरुम् ॥१॥
प्रथमं ज्ञानदेवादीन् कवीरादींस्ततः परम् ।
व्याख्यातुं वसवादीश्च सोऽवातरन्महीतले ॥२॥
उमदीमुनिशिष्यो यो निम्बर्गीमतशङ्करः ।
सन्तो वर्दान्त सर्वे तं भक्तवाणीविनायकम् ॥३॥
प्रणीतं सन्निधौ तस्य मया रेदासदर्शनम् ।
सम्पादितं च भाषायां रानडेदर्शनं पुनः ॥४॥
द्रष्टुं ज्ञातुं परं तत्त्वं रानडेजीवनं तथा ।
अल साधकसर्वस्वं रानडेदर्शनं मम ॥५॥

(1)

Between 1952 and 1956 I was in the close contact of Prof. R. D. Ranade. He used to come to stay at Allahabad every year from January or February to April and May. During

his stay I was privileged to meet him almost every day. So I got the opportunity of holding numerous sittings with him. But in each sitting I found him in new perspectives. The spirit in him was ever new. It was difficult to understand him completely. The only gain was, that I got a new inspiration to meet him again. Each encounter with his personality invariably led to another. Such was the magnetic attraction in it !

Today he is no more in his earthly coil. But still I continue to see him, or rather remember him, as I used to do during the fifties. Indeed hardly a day passes off when I do not see him in his meditation pose. His personality is, undoubtedly, immortal, not only because it is enshrined in his immortal works, but also because it is living in the lives of his numerous followers and disciples. I fully subscribe to the view of the great Hindi saint. Nabhadasa who says in his *Bhaktamālā* that love for God, the man who has this love, God and the teacher of the man—these four constitute one single personality. So wherever there is love for God initiated by Prof. Ranade or his disciples, there he is living in the very form his earthly existence signified. The continuity of his spiritual tradition, message and meditation has made him immortal in the true sense of the word. Those who nave this sense can see him even now.

(II)

I have many experiences about him and it is not possible to record all of them here. So I shall describe only two or three of them and leave the rest for some future occasions. Prof. Ranade had attained to the state of desirelessness. There was no trace of any desire or longing in him. He did not suffer even from the last infirmity of human mind, viz Love for fame. When Prof. S. Radhakrishnan became the Vice-President of India, I asked him to comment on his

appointment. He expressed his happiness over it and said that it augured well for the good of the nation. But when I asked him whether he himself wished to be the Vice-President or President of India, he replied emphatically in the negative and said, "I have dedicated my life to God-realization. Is there anything more valuable? why do you think of the undesirable?"

These talks with Prof. Ranade have revealed to me one thing, inter alia, that he was completely committed to philosophy and religion. Whereas his contemporaries and colleagues sought the reward of their services to philosophy and religion and left philosophy for political and social work, he did not do so, for, he was above the State. He was in the line of Indian Rishis and saints that were not enamoured of State and its power.

Such was his love for philosophy. I have yet to come across a teacher of philosophy who is as devoted to philosophy as Prof Ranade was. In fact he was philosophy incarnate. who-soever came in his contact became a philosopher in his own right. To know him was to know philosophy. To know the philosopher was to be a philosopher. *Brahma Veda Brahmaiva Bhavati.*

(15)

## **A Renowned Philosopher-Saint**

( *By : Sri K. P. Kulkarni* )

One of our popular professors was Shri Rambhau Ranade. He taught us Carlyle's 'Heroes'. The town Kolhapur was a common bond that had fostered between us a sense of reciprocal kinship. Shri Bapurao Ranade, his step-brother, was a teacher to all of us and Rambhau made frequent trips to Kolhapur to meet him. Rambhau was also the maternal uncle of Narahari Damle, one of our close circle. At every University examination, Rambhau used to rank first and make a rich haul of prizes and scholarships. Naturally every one of his visits to the Damle's drew us thither in curiosity as well as admiration. Of course in the heart of hearts we were making mental notes all the while of the ideal scholar's style of walk and talk, his general turn out, his bearing, his fads and what not ! Being with him, at least for a while, was a matter of self-gratulation for us. That year particularly Rambhau had secured the much coveted Chancellor's Gold Medal for philosophy at the M. A. examination. Fergusson College, therefore, held for us the dual attraction of Dr. Gune and

Rambhau Ranade, Sharp of intellect, sweet in nature and unassuming in disposition he always impressed one at first sight. He was a personification of good nature. Physically however he looked somewhat frail But his profound erudition more than compensated this shortcoming. He used to be dressed in a very simple style. A clean bright 'dhoti', a pair of typical red Poona slippers (जोड़ा), a loose none-too fashionable shirt with thread buttons, a spacious tight collared shortish coat buttoned up straight, a fairly long muslin muffler (उपरणे) slung casually around the neck, a liberal saffron coloured paste mark on the yawning forehead, a headgear (pugree) typical of Poona perched at ease and indifferent on the crest, and baggy dark gown rather shuffling about in careless defiance of all order—in such a uniform. if it could be called one, he used to enter the classroom walking unusually fast. Sometimes he carried a book or two extra in his hand while going to the class. The projection of his personality would easily profess the subject he taught—philosophy. From the moment he entered the classroom the stream of his eloquence flowed unfaltered till the bell tolled signifying the closure of the hour. The English he spoke was pitched low but delivered fast and was profound yet lucid. It was packed with meaning cast in classical mould, and somewhat ponderous yet within easy grasp of the student. It had about it the sanctity and majesty of the Ganges Everytime the student felt unmistakably that, he had heard something novel and extraordinary, that he had made a successful sojourn into the realm of the unknowable and that it was a charmed moment that had yielded some rare acquisition, an experience bordering on the ecstatic. There was a special Ranade touch about everything of his—unfolding the depth of Carlyle's thoughts or his superbly fluent eloquence, the uncanny tact of making the student gravitate towards him, the magic touch inducing love of literature in the student, and the masterly way of re-establishing the ancient tie of the teacher and the taught which seemed to mock at the

heterodox spirit of modernity. The impression that he made on us then stands out in bold relief even now, after a lapse of fortyfive years.

### The Upanishadic Sage :

Often Ranade asked the students to write essays and after going through them he returned them to the students with his own comments, suggestions and opinions, pointing out mistakes therein, if any. At times he also called them home for discussions over the subject matter of the essays. He had two spacious rooms constructed just beyond the Fergusson college Hostel; while his family residence was in Shaniwar Peth. Ranade often spent long studious hours in these rooms. We had nicknamed them as Carlyle Cottage. Students considered it a rare honour and privilege whenever they were summoned by Rambhau Ranade for discussions. By temperament Rambhau was a person of transparent candour. With a childlike innocence he used to mix with students shaking off typical aloofness, teachers are normally prone to maintain. This in turn imposed on the students a sense of embarrassment and awkwardness which compelled them to talk some garbled stuff, sitting under great constraint. At the cottage he looked a veritable skeleton of skin and bones flitting about in his 'dhoti' with its back strip amusingly shaggy and the bulging loops and falls in front helplessly dragging along and with his hair-lock a-top the crown, jumping about in unintentional mischief. Looking at him one felt one was squatting before some archaic Rshi for a session of sermons. Rangarao Diwakar (who later became the Governor of Bihar) was one of his favourite pupils. Like him many others whose essays earned his appreciation received invitations to the cottage from him. Once I too had the good fortune to receive it.

### The Saint of Nimbal

I was once summoned by Dr. Ranade to Nimbal in

connection with the examination of a thesis of my student. I arrived in Nimbal at about eight in the night. My host had already made careful arrangements to despatch one person to the station to receive me and have me lodged comfortably. About 10 o' clock at night Rambhau called on me at my room and as soon as he saw me he expressed his pleasant surprise saying, " Oh ! Is that you Mr. Kulkarni ! Well, I know, he is my student, a Fergussonian ! I still remember very clearly that excellent essay of his. " I was dumbfounded. A strange mixture of joy, gratitude and several undiscernible sentiments filled me. After brief formalities he left. I was very happy to extend my stay there for two more days in the enchanting, beatific atmosphere charged with the holiness of the saint Rambhau Ranade. When I left I had the contentment of a fulfilled mission

(16)
An Ideal Guru.

( *By : Surendra Prasad Garg* )

In 1952 I was introduced to Shri Gurudev Ranade Maharaj & went to Nimbal for his blessed *darshan*. By that time I had not been initiated and was against this tradition of Guru worship. When the disciples of Shri Gurudev recited verses in praise of Shri Gurudev & prostrated to pay respects to him, I did not approve of it & a number of doubts about the qualification of a Guru arose in my mind. It was a most lucky hour when Shri Gurudev gave a ring and all the disciples and devotees gathered in the hall and Shri Gurudev delivered his Pravachan on the qualities of a Guru without my asking this question to him. He said that a Guru must have the following qualifications :

- 1. He should be himself a self-realised soul having a deep insight in the *Shāshtrās*.
- 2. Secondly a real Guru need not expect any thing from his disciples. He should look to the welfare of his devotees.
- 3. Thirdly, the personal life of a Guru should be above board and should accord to the injunctions of the sacred books.

He need not indulge in any practices not recommended by the *Shāshtrās* on the plea that he is omni-potent.

4. A Guru is omni-scient, all-powerful like God and he should be bestowing both worldly & spiritual benefits on his disciples.

On hearing this *pravachan* of Shri Ranade Maharaj, I, immediately decided to get myself initiated by him. I was lucky to receive initiation next morning.

In the afternoon, it so happened that the disciples & devotees were sitting for meditation along with Shri Gurudev. By an accident, the thunder struck upon the roof of the hall, went penetrating to the ground touching the head of one of the disciples. It was really a very horrible & frightening incident but none of the persons in meditation was affected. All kept on sitting silently for the duration of the meditation. At the end of an hour Shri Ranade Maharaj merely enquired about the matter and adviced measures conducting electricity to earth. He was quite indifferent to the happening.

The food served to the devotees was quite simple and Shri Gurudev used to bless it by looking at it, before it was served. He himself was a very abstemious eater & advised that minimum quality of food should be taken. Otherwise one will not be able to sit in meditation for a long time.

At that time I had been unjustly demoted to the post of Tehsildar after working as Sub-Divisional Officer & Assistant Secretary to the Government for about four years. When I was about to depart from the Ashram, Shri Gurudev of his own accord asked me when I would become an Assistant Collector i. e. S. D. O. What reply I could give to this question? But soon after my return from the Ashram, I was unexpectedly promoted to the post of Assistant Collector. It was only due to grace of Shri Gurudev. Even today, though I have to face a

number of difficulties in life, now & then. But they get resolved and eventually I find myself in quite easy circumstances, and have no liabilities & worries which generally travel a worldly person. It is all due to Shri Gurudev, who is always alive and takes due care of his disciples & devotees. I am quite sure that the grace of Shri Gurudev will grant me love of God & lead to Bhagwan after this *sthool* body dissolves.

(17)

**He Lived Paramartha**

( *By : Dr. P. D. Khanolkar* )

Dr. R. D. Ranade— a great mystic philosopher and a Spiritual teacher. ( *Sudguru* ) to a large number of aspirants in the South and also in the North attained *Samādhi* at Nimbal in his *Āśhram*, which has been a place of enlightenment to the seekers for the last two decades and more, in Bijapur District, on 6-6-1977 and thus a great void is created in the minds of many of his followers. I myself all along under his spiritual guidance, came not only to revere him but to take him as a father. His was a child-like simplicity and earnestness of purpose. He conveyed spiritual truths to us in an effective manner. His great attachment to all of his *Sādhakās* and persons who came into his contact was remarkable. He made no distinction between any of his followers. He was always found dancing to the tune of the 'Maker' completely forgetful of worldly surroundings. He was one with Divinity. Every one found something new in the way of his approach to *Sādhakās*' problems. Their spiritual and material welfare was always his first concern. Such a

dynamic personality He was.

Since last July (1956) he was gradually retreating from the world, and since March (1957) he was seen utterly detached from the world, always unmindful of environments. He developed acute Bronchitis which was gradually complicated into Bronchiectasis. He never took any medicine except some sedative linctus which did not interfere with his process of meditation. During his life time also, there were occasions of his grave illness when the doctors attending him and the people near to him were very much anxious about his life; but to their wonder '*Gurudeo*', on the strength of his spiritual powers, recovered successfully and thus the Medicos were left baffled. I had the good fortune of examining *Sri Gurudeo Ranade* just after his recent return from Allahabad to Nimbal on 30-4-1957 and I found on X'ray examination on 2-5-1957 at Nimbal that he had old-healed Tubercular lesions in both spices of the lungs and a patch of haziness on the Right Costophrenic angle, which also disappeared after about 12 days. His pulse was varying from 90 to 110 and he had irritant cough due to laryngitis. He was slowly getting emaciated. When he last came to me to Sholapur on 16-5-1957 and upon my request he consented to get X'rayed, and to my great surprise. I found that both the lungs were clear and the Rt. lower lobe showed Honey-combed appearance with markedly prominent hilar shadows, without taking any antibiotic treatment usually prescribed for such diseases. I explained to him the whole position of his illness. His dry hacking cough with severe laryngitis continued. Lungs were not showing any sign except a few rales (moist sounds). He was examined by a number of other eminent Doctors who also came to the conclusion that his Bronchiectasis also was clearing off both clinically and radiologically. In the end, His temperature subsided but he was markedly asthenic due to starvation. He developed aphonia and used to express his thoughts by signs. His breathing was perfectly regular and pulse was steady. His sputum was negative for acid fast organism throughout.

During the last 5 days before his departure (*Niryān*) he was completely detached from the world. He particularly got himself thoroughly examined 12 hours before he left his body, i-e, on 6th June 1957 at 10-30 A.M. by Dr. N. S. Paripatyagar of Sholapur as if, it seemed, to get confirmed that he was completely free from any disease. During those last 5 days he did not take even a morsel of food or a drop of water but took particular care to get his bowels cleared by laxative. The Doctor on examination found the lungs clear and he did not find any other abnormality except extreme asthenia and it was astonishing for him to see that no faecal matter was lodged in the colon.

Revered Gurudeo, however, took his last sip of water just before. His gracious soul left the physique at 10-30 P. M to console *Śrīmati* Kakusaheb (Mrs. Ranade) on her pathetic appeal to Him as He was fully conscious to the last breath.

Thus the revered and elevated Soul departed with a complete control over his disease, giving up the clear body back to the Creater, in the same way as did '*Kabir*' offer his body (*Chaddar*) unmolsted to 'GOD'.

“दास कबीर जतन करि ओढि । ज्यो त्यो घर दीनी चदरिया”

  as was also done by the great Saint of *Karnatak*, *Śri Nimbargi Maharaj* when he said :

“अप्पा गुरुराया निन्नदु निनगे ओष्पितु ”

  meaning, “ O Lord, the body given by you is handed over back to you as (pure as) it was.

Even after death, His body remained perfectly lustrous without any sign of *rigor Mortis or post mortem* lividity for the next 18 hours till the final holy rites. I noticed with astonishment that the tip of His nose was particularly shining and His iris was partially devoid of pigment and conjunctive, lustrous whitish in colour.

The revered Soul passed away in a joyous enjoyment of 'God' deeply engrossed in meditation and completely away from the material world, leaving behind Him, His great immortal works, on realisation of God, with full of practical experiences. He synthesised both East and West in devotional, spiritual, and mystic aspects of philosophy, having full faith and reliance on higher Forces.

*Gurudeo Dr. Ranade* lived 'Paramārth' throughout his life. A minute observation of the Saint's life would reveal that the beginning and culmination of his life was spiritualism-realization of God ( *Swaroop* - *Sāksātkār* ). He used to say "Spiritualism has been the aim of my life; let it be its culmination also." *Sri Gurudeo Ranade*, the mystic saint, impressed the value of *Subeej Nāma* and meditation on the name of God imparted by a God-realised saint, the simplest and yet the most dynamic way of spiritual realisation in the present world of strife and struggle for existence. By practising 'Sādhana' for over 50 years, he showed to the present world, full of distress and miseries, that meditation alone is the easiest and the surest way of attainment of God-realisation and spiritual happiness. The essential requisites, he stressed, as did the great saints of the past and the ancient Seers of yore (lkśīs), were the cultivation of moral virtues and elimination of vices and bad qualities, coupled with God-love and God-devotion and *Satsang*, before spiritual life could be fully realised. As a result of his dynamic personality, people from all classes and from all spheres of life, were attracted to him and revered him as their Spiritual Teacher'-*Sadguru*.' Thus this divine personality blessed hundreds of aspirants with the holy 'Mantra' (*Name*), ever guiding them on the Pathway to God.

(18)

## **Gurudeva as a Spiritual Gardener**

( *By : Sri S. N. Deshpande* )

‘ *Nāma* is a symbol that carries divine power with it and Its *Smaraṇa* is a process of constant identification with God ’ exclaimed *Gurudeva* in one of his post-ecstatic monologues. His one pointed Divine personality could be perceived in a cross-section of his whole life as depicted in this cryptic but vibrant expression pregnant with his philosophy of the Spirit.

When I was first blessed by *Gurudeva* with an intimate interview in June 1934, I was beyond myself with a sense of exhileration, gratification and sublimation in life. Even before I entered the four walls of his holy abode of meditation at *Nimbāl*, the repeated thrilling musical exclamations of the Divine Name ‘ *Nārāyaṇa Nārāyaṇa Nārāyaṇa* ’ maddened my soul as these God-intoxicated utterances penetrated my heart like the sudden flash of a rumbling column of light from the blue. The inexperienced young boy of twenty in me became extremely impatient and eager to see in person, the unseen

and unknown personality of *Gurudeva*. In my childish fancy I had mentally painted my own picture of *Gurudeva* as a tall, stout and an impressive figure like that of *Swāmi Vivekānānd*. Within a few moments I was surprisingly disillusioned to perceive a thin, lean and an emaciated figure of *Gurudeva* looking like a mere bony skeleton wrapped with lustrous silky skin. The fragrance and the splendour of his spiritual self was ebbing out of his glowing looks and his soothing words which in course of time, bathed me in unique compassion, love, kindness and inspiration never before experienced in my life. The child in me felt that it has regained its long lost mother.

I was on the threshold of joining the Agricultural College for shaping my academic career in life. After a few words of introductory talk, *Gurudeva* suddenly and most unexpectedly referred to my plan of joining the Agricultural College and endorsed the idea with the following thoughts. In the words of *Curlyle*, he advised us to become peasant saints. To earn the bread for the body we have to take to agriculture and to cater to the needs and aspirations of the spirit, we have to cultivate saintliness and reap the harvest of life Divine. Hence agriculture and the culture of the spirit should form the two pillars of evolution of the body and the soul simultaneously.

Just as the peasant toils day in and day out to cultivate his land and add to the fertility of the soil, the saint in man has to keep a constant vigil on the Name of God, day and night, and make his encased self worthy of a flight into the fathomless fermarient of the Divine Cosmos.

The double personality of a peasant and a saint in man has to grow side by side, in a homogeneous manner, reciprocally complimentary to each other. The human vehicle in flesh and blood has to develop as a peasant up to a certain limit,

only to outgrow the bonds of human limitations and transfigure itself into a vehicle of the Divine will. The agriculture has to sublimate itself into the culture and nurture of the spirit in man for the evolution of the individual self. This is possible only through a theo-centric process of surrender of the lower self and an unfoldment of a continuous awareness of the Divine Name and Form. Just as the vital process of breathing goes on reflexively inspite of our utter neglect and unawareness of the basic fact that sustains the spirit in this tenament of the flesh, so also the descending of the Divine Grace and mercy is continuous, inspite of human ignorance, neglect and indifference. The culture of the spirit sets in, when through the blessings of saints like *Gurudeva* the individual self catches the current of awareness of the Divine Name, and reciprocally attempts to ascend the ladder of spiritual life, to mingle with the descending Grace of the Divine. Then this process of spiritual awareness becomes as automatic and reflex as the act of physical breathing.

For inculcating in our daily life, the awareness of this double process of descent of the divine Grace and ascent of a devotee, through the method of meditation and dedication, we may be benefited by the guide lines suggested by *Gurudeva Ranade*, as a spiritual Gardener. In this context *Gurudeva* compared the growth of a plant with that of the sprouting of a seed of Divine Name, in the heart of a devotee. The growth of the seed and the seedling depends mainly on three factors. The innate potency of the seed to grow, the timely plantation in a well-cultivated and manured soil, and the opportune watering of the roots and the shoots after eradication of the weeds. It is the deepening growth of the unseen roots under ground that result in the exhuberance of the foliage above. The huge variety of colour, flower, fragrance and quality of flowers and fruits proclaim to the world the limitless and unimaginable power of the Divine Energy.

The critical knowledge and observation of *Gurudeva*

as a botanist and plant-pathologist could enable him to elucidate the comparison in deeper details. Meditation on the name of God, is like watering the roots of the plant and reading the spiritual literature and singing the glory of God are similar to the process of sprinkling the water on the foliage and branches of the plant, to regulate the process of transpiration. If the roots do not get the timely supply of water, the plant will not survive and if the process of transpiration is not regulated through external sprinkling of water, the excess evaporation of the water content will weaken the progress of the plant growth. Thus the relative importance of both the meditation and the singing of prayers and *bhajans* is made clear by the gardener in *Gurudeva*.

The imposing construction of *Gurudeva Mandir* with a huge garden round about, on the out-skirts of *Belgaum* reminds me of the fundamentals of spiritual gardening as proposed by *Gurudeva*. An ardent prayer springs up in the solitude of my humble heart that the Spiritual Gardener may guide us on the right path to fulfil the purpose of गुरुदेव मंदीर— Gurudeva Mandir.

(19)

**His Supernatural Power**

( By : V. S. Page )

Following is the faithful account of an incident that took place at Sangli, which I described while giving a brief talk at the Academy of Comparative Philosophy and Religion, Belgaum, when I visited it last. ☞

I attended a ceremony at Sangli in Ganpati Mandir when Gurudev Dr. R. D. Ranade and Dr. Radhakrishnan were present. Dr. Radhakrishnan was then the President of India. Thereafter, somehow, I was called to the Mal bungalow, a palace of the Rajesaheb of Sangli, by Shri Gurudev. I was specially called to place my views before him regarding Vedant philosophy, as given by Nischaldas, in his book Vicharsagar. This was because, I guess, somebody must have whispered into his ear about me. I was a bit surprised at this call. I was called at 3-00 p. m. in the Mal Bungalow. Accordingly I went

☞ Shri Page paid a visit to Gurudev Mandir, Belgaum on Makar-Sankrant day ( 14-1-1973 )

there My maternal uncle, late Shri D. M. Varadkar, was with me. When I went there I found that Shri Gurudev was closetted in a room and was deeply immersed in writing something. The devotees sitting outside the room told me that nothing could be sure about his coming out though he had called me at 3-00 p. m. However, exactly at 3-00 p. m. Shri Gurudev came out. Though I had seen him many times earlier, the pose in which I saw him was rather startling. I was amazed at his mannerism. He held a pick-dan, a utensil for spitting, in his right hand. Under his left arm-pit there was a bundle of shirts. Perhaps, he wanted to change shirts within a short span of time. He wore dhoti in a loose fashion. As soon as he came out he asked me, "Are you Mr. Page?" I said. "Yes, I am Page." A thought crossed my mind as I was looking at him. I thought: Is this a learned man whose manners seem to be quite eccentric, if not anything else? He started going out along with me to the main hall in the palace. As soon as the thought mentioned above crossed my mind he looked at me, almost stared at me, and asked me a question, "Have you read 'Contemporary Philosophers', a Government of India publication?" I said, "No, I have not read it." He said, "Read it." I asked, "What I am supposed to read in it; what in particular?" Shri Gurudev said, "I have written an article in it. Do read that article. You will find answers to your questions." Then I was silent. I need not tell what happened thereafter. We went in the main hall. I gave a brief talk. Shri Gurudev was very much pleased to hear me and he encouraged me by words of blessings. He told me that exposition of Vedant doctrines. as I gave, was very correct and he was pleased with my talk. Thereafter I returned home. I then procured the book he asked me to read. I read his article. There I found the explanation of his mannerism. A reader can profitably go through that article. In short, the reason for his behaviour is given by Dnyaneshwar in his commentary on Geeta, briefly. "वेडिवे माजी देडे महिमे भेणे", I hope I need not write much.
